# Bes Email Dispatch

Handler skill for the email-forwarding workflow. Justin forwards an email to `goff.justin+bes@gmail.com` with a one-line instruction at the top of the body (or just a subject prefix); a Gmail filter labels it `Bes/Inbox`; a poller (`poll_bes_inbox.py`) detects it and invokes this skill once per new message ID.

This skill is **read-only on Gmail**. It never archives, marks read, or replies. The source of truth for "has Bes seen this?" is the watermark file (`~/.hermes/state/bes-inbox-watermark.json`), not Gmail label state.

## Inputs

One Gmail message ID. The poller passes it via the cron prompt; you call `scripts/load_context.py <id>` to fetch.

## Core Principle: Tweakable Dual-Action Dispatch

When Justin forwards an email, he wants one of two actions (or sometimes both) to happen based on keywords and context in his one-line instruction (`instruction` field from `load_context.py`):

1. **Add the email to his Obsidian Vault (File it)**
2. **Create a Todoist task based on the email (Task it)**

For each action, Justin will include keywords and some context on the instruction line, for example:
- *File this. I like the idea about the flux capacitor. I wonder if we could use it for the improbablity engine.*
- *Task due Friday. Gotta finish the book before the weekend.*
- *TODO due tomorrow. Check with Anya.*

If his instruction contains keywords for **both** (or if he lists them on separate lines/sentences), you must perform **both** actions!

See [references/forwarding-examples.md](references/forwarding-examples.md) for concrete mockups of instruction inputs and expected tool outputs.

### Default Behavior (Fallback)
If the instruction is empty, has no keywords, or is just "Save as a note", default to **Action 1: Add the email to his vault**.

---

## Action 1: File Email (Save to Vault Inbox)

### Trigger Keywords
- Contains: `File this`, `file this`, `file`, `save this`, `save`, `archive this`
- Or: Instruction is **empty / none** (default fallback, files to `Inbox/`)

### Storage Destination
- Create a new markdown note inside the **`Inbox/`** directory of his vault:
  `/home/justin.guest/vault/Inbox/YYYY-MM-DD-subject-slug.md`
  *(Where `YYYY-MM-DD` is the current date or forwarded email date, and `subject-slug` is a cleaned, lowercase, hyphen-separated version of the cleaned subject).*

### Note Structure & Frontmatter
All new notes must start with the `New Note` frontmatter (pre-evaluating Templater values at write time using Justin's local time (America/New_York)):

```yaml
---
id: "<YYYYMMDDHHmmss at write time, e.g. 20260520143157>"
daily_note: "[[<YYYY-MM-DD Weekday>|YYYY-MM-DD Weekday]]"
---
```

Below the frontmatter, format the note body cleanly:
1. **Title:** Large H1 heading `# [Cleaned Subject]`
2. **Email Metadata:** Labeled key-value pairs:
   - **From:** [Original Sender Name <Email>]
   - **To:** [Recipient Email]
   - **Date:** [Original Email Date]
3. **Context Note:** If Justin provided an instruction or extra thoughts (e.g., "I like the idea about the flux capacitor..."), include them in a `## Context` section.
4. **Summary:** Add a concise markdown summary of the email's content (who sent it, what it is about).
5. **Email Content:** A `---` line or `## Email Content` header followed by the cleaned plaintext body of the forwarded email.

---

## Action 1b: Log Email (Save to Inputs/Emails/)

### Trigger Keywords
- Contains: `log this`, `log email`, `log thread`, `save as email log`, `log`

### Storage Destination
- Create a new markdown note inside **`Inputs/Emails/`** (`$OBSIDIAN_VAULT_PATH/Inputs/Emails/YYYY-MM-DD - Spaced Subject.md`)
  *(Where `YYYY-MM-DD` is the current date, and `Spaced Subject` is a cleaned, capitalized, spaced version of the subject).*

### Note Structure & Frontmatter
All new email log notes must start with this frontmatter format:

```yaml
---
id: "<YYYYMMDDHHmmss at write time>"
daily_note: "[[<YYYY-MM-DD Weekday>|YYYY-MM-DD Weekday]]"
category: "[[Emails]]"
type: email
original_url: "<Gmail message search link, e.g. https://mail.google.com/mail/u/0/#search/rfc822msgid:<Message-ID> or search query>"
---
```

Below the frontmatter, format the note body cleanly:
1. **Title:** Large H1 heading `# 📧 Email Log: [Cleaned Subject]`
2. **Email Metadata:** Labeled key-value pairs:
   - **From:** [Original Sender Name <Email>]
   - **Date:** [Original Email Date]
   - **Subject:** [Cleaned Subject]
   - **Message ID:** [Gmail Message ID] (to fetch full email if needed)
3. **Context Note:** If Justin provided any instruction or extra thoughts, include them in a `## Context` section.
4. **Summary:** Add a brief summary of the entire thread (concise bullets or paragraph outlining key discussions, decisions, and action items — **do not copy the email contents verbatim**).

---

## Action 2: Create a Todoist Task

### Trigger Keywords
- Contains: `Task`, `task`, `TODO`, `todo`, `to do`, `To do`

### Task Creation Specifications
Use `mcp_todoist_add_tasks` to add a single task to Justin's Todoist **Inbox** (projectId: `"6VGcQ7r6HW5r87j9"` or `"inbox"`):

1. **Task Name (`content`):** Determine a meaningful, clear, actionable name based on the email's subject and summary. Do NOT use the raw `Fwd: ...` subject or a generic name.
2. **Task Description (`description`):** Append whatever contextual note Justin has given you to the end of the task description (e.g. `Gotta finish the book before the weekend.`).
3. **Due Date (`dueString`):** Extract any due date specified in the instruction (e.g., "due Friday", "due tomorrow", "due 6/15"). Pass this as the `dueString` parameter of the task. If no due date is mentioned, omit the `dueString` parameter.
4. **Comment on Task:** After creating the task, immediately call `mcp_todoist_add_comments` to add a comment containing a concise summary of the email, including the original sender, recipient, and date. This keeps the task neat while preserving the original context.

---

## Other Intent Shapes (Legacy Support)

If Justin explicitly uses the following phrasing, support these specific paths:
- **Person note:** *"Person note for <Name>"* or *"<Name> works at <Org>"* → Create a brand-new Person note named `<Capitalized Spaced Full Name>.md` in `/home/justin.guest/vault/Inbox/` (or update the existing note in-place if it already exists under `/Contacts/` or `/Inbox/`).
- **Company/Organization note:** *"New company <Name>"*, *"Company note for <Name>"*, or *"<Name> is a new company"* → Create a brand-new Organization note named `<Capitalized Spaced Name>.md` in `/home/justin.guest/vault/Inbox/` (or update the existing note in-place if it already exists under `/Contacts/` or `/Inbox/`).
- **Project note:** *"New project <Name>"*, *"Project note for <Name>"*, or *"<Name> is a new project"* → Create `<lowercase-name-slug>.md` under `projects/` using Project formatting (executive summary, Status: Active, and creation Timeline).
- **Append to existing note:** *"Add to <note title>"*, *"Append to <note title>"*, or *"Add [content] to the <note title> note"* → Find the closest match vault-wide (the user may say "in my inbox" or guess the wrong folder, but the note often resides in its correct MECE directory like `personal/trips/` or `projects/`) and append a dated bullet point (format: `- YYYY-MM-DD | Ingest — <context/details>`).
- **Calendar scheduling:** *"Schedule this"* or *"Add this to my calendar"* → Parse event details and call `gws_multi.py --account personal-main|work calendar create`.

---

## Process Workflow

For each message ID detected by the poller:

1. **Load context:** Run `load_context.py <MESSAGE_ID>` to get the JSON email payload.
2. **Determine intents:** Scan the `instruction` string for trigger keywords to decide if you need to:
   - File the email to Vault (`File this` / `save` / empty)
   - Create a Todoist task (`Task` / `TODO` / `to do`)
   - Or both!
3. **Execute actions:**
   - If filing: Generate and write the markdown note to `Inbox/` or `Inputs/Emails/`.
   - After filing, run `llm-wiki` integrate-light: append `Utilities/log.md` only (daily note wikilink as last field).
   - If creating a task: Call `mcp_todoist_add_tasks` and then `mcp_todoist_add_comments` with the email summary.
   - If both: Do both operations.
4. **Report back:** Output a single concise line per email in your final response (for Telegram delivery):
   - `✅ <subject snippet> → filed to vault and created Todoist task "<task_name>"`
   - `✅ <subject snippet> → filed to vault as <filename>.md`
   - `✅ <subject snippet> → created Todoist task "<task_name>"`
   - `❌ <subject snippet> → load_context failed (is_real=false). Skipping.`

---

## Guidelines & Rules

- **Verify Writes:** After writing any note to the vault, verify the file exists and is non-empty before reporting success.
- **Avoid Loop Guards:** Skip any emails sent by Bes himself to prevent infinite loops.
- **Rate Limit:** Limit processing to at most 5 emails per cron tick. If there are more, report that the rest will be picked up next tick.

## Troubleshooting & Pitfalls

- **Empty plaintext parts in HTML emails:** Some systems/senders (like Expedia transactional emails) send `multipart/alternative` messages with a nearly empty text/plain part containing only `\r\n` (whitespace). Because `google_api.py` previously checked `if not body:`, this truthy whitespace caused it to skip extracting the actual HTML content. Always ensure `google_api.py` checks `if not body.strip():` when extracting bodies to correctly fall back to the rich HTML content.

The user has provided the following instruction alongside the skill invocation: [IMPORTANT: You are running as a scheduled cron job. DELIVERY: Your final response will be automatically delivered to the user — do NOT use send_message or try to deliver the output yourself. Just produce your report/output as your final response and the system handles the rest. SILENT: If there is genuinely nothing new to report, respond with exactly "[SILENT]" (nothing else) to suppress delivery. Never combine [SILENT] with content — either report your findings normally, or say [SILENT] and nothing more.]

Do not dump the entire session at once.\\n- Wait for Justin's explicit go-ahead or text response between phases.\\n\\n## Pitfalls & Defensive Rules\\n\\n- **Preserve the Notepad:** Always load today's daily note first, find the `## \ud83d\uddd2 Notepad` section, and keep its contents completely intact.\\n- **Inputs Terminology:** Always refer to Slack threads, emails, and other primary-category sources as \\\"inputs\\\" rather than \\\"logs\\\" in both conversations and note frontmatter, as per the updated vault schema.\\n- **Accurate Attribution:** When drafting highlights and decisions from emails or meeting notes, ensure decisions are attributed to the correct person (e.g., Anya, Nana, teachers, etc.) rather than assuming Justin made them.\\n- **Escape Slack Channels:** Always write `#channel-name` as `\\\\#channel-name` inside the daily note so Obsidian doesn't parse it as a tag.\\n- **Dynamic Timezone Offset:** When fetching calendar events, always calculate and append the local timezone offset (e.g. `-04:00` or `-05:00`) to `--start` and `--end` to prevent boundary events from leaking from yesterday or tomorrow.\\n- **Git Commit Warning:** Do not manually `git add` or `git commit` any vault edits. The `bes-vault-sync` watcher will handle it immediately.\\n- **Todoist Task Creation Rule:** When creating any Todoist task, always add a one-sentence comment immediately after \u2014 source + why it became a task.\\n- **Todoist Filter Preference:** Do not present tasks using native Todoist sidebar views (Today, Inbox, etc.), as Justin finds them cluttered. Emphasize saved filter views.\\n- **Frontmatter Safety & Infinite Loops:** Avoid extracting body content in a way that includes leading newlines, preventing infinite overwrite loops during hygiene tasks. Always `.lstrip()` body content immediately upon extraction.\\n- **Dangling Closing Dividers:** Ensure any automated or manual procedure that adds or updates properties writes back the closing divider (`---`) on a *fresh line*. Writing it without an intervening newline will append it directly to the end of the last property string (e.g., `daily_note: '...'---`), which corrupts properties.\\n- **Non-Unique Aliases Guard:** Always skip auto-linking any alias that is non-unique (shared by more than one distinct contact path) to avoid incorrect connections in the vault.\\n- **Timelines Deactivation (manual wind-down):** Do not manually append `## Timeline` bullets to contact cards during wind-down; rely on Obsidian's native Backlinks panel instead. **`integrate-entities`** is the sanctioned automated append path for both contacts and projects at ingest time \u2014 cron and meeting reconcile use it.\\n- **Open Loops File:** Do not modify the `/home/justin.guest/vault/Open Loops.md` file directly. No, based on a deep dive into our PostHog data and codebase, **this is NOT working as expected today.**\\\\n\\\\nWhile the property is set for a tiny fraction of users (~1.1% of active users, or exactly 1,018 users out of the 90,954 who completed the onboarding motivation questionnaire in the last 30 days), it is completely missing for the other 99%. Furthermore, there is **not a single user on iOS** who has ever had this property successfully set in PostHog.\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n### \\\\ud83d\\\\udd0d Why is this happening?\\\\n\\\\nOur investigation revealed two distinct issues in the current implementation:\\\\n\\\\n1. **Async Initialization Race Condition (The iOS Gap)**\\\\n   On mobile, the PostHog React Native SDK is initialized asynchronously via a `setTimeout` in `initPostHogApp.ts`. When a user answers the very first onboarding questionnaire step (`why-here`), `global.PostHog` is still loading and is undefined.\\\\n   - While `logEventPostHog` safely queues the `'question_answered'` event inside `libraryLoadQueue` to send once ready, the separate call to `global.PostHog?.setPersonProperties?.(...)` in `logQuestionAnswered.ts` is executed immediately, silently falls back (optional chaining), and is **never queued or retried**.\\\\n   - Because Android loading/timing differs slightly, about 1,029 Android users successfully hit the call. On iOS, 100% of these calls silently dropped.\\\\n\\\\n2. **Anonymous vs Identified Profiles (`personProfiles: 'identifiedOnly'`)**\\\\n   Onboarding happens before sign up/login, so users are **anonymous** when answering. Because our PostHog project is configured with `personProfiles: 'identifiedOnly'`, any `$set` person property events sent for anonymous users do not create profiles and are dropped. When the user later registers and we call `posthog.identify()`, we send `onb_reasons_for_learning` (via `identifyUser.ts`) but we never synchronize or send `learning_reason`, so it is lost for good.\\\\n\\\\n---\\\\n\\\\n### \\\\ud83d\\\\udee0\\\\ufe0f Proposed Solution\\\\n\\\\nWe can resolve both issues completely with a robust, two-pronged fix in the codebase:\\\\n\\\\n#### 1. Attach `$set` directly to the event payload (Fixes timing & iOS)\\\\nIn `client/app/state/analytics/eventsPosthog/torEvents/questionScreen/logQuestionAnswered.ts`, instead of a separate `setPersonProperties` call, attach `$set: { learning_reason: params.answer_texts }` directly to the `question_answered` event payload itself:\\\\n\\\\n```typescript\\\\n\\\\tif (params.question_id === 'why-here') {\\\\n\\\\t\\\\tparams.$set = { learning_reason: params.answer_texts }\\\\n\\\\t}\\\\n\\\\n\\\\tlogEventPostHog('question_answered', params)\\\\n```\\\\nSince the event is queued in `libraryLoadQueue` if PostHog is not ready, the property will ride with the event and successfully set when the queue flushes.\\\\n\\\\n#### 2. Synchronize on identification (Fixes anonymous profiles)\\\\nIn `client/app/state/analytics/identify/identifyUser.ts`, set `learning_reason` directly alongside `onb_reasons_for_learning` so it gets explicitly persisted to their identified person profile post-auth:\\\\n\\\\n```typescript\\\\n\\\\t\\\\tconst reasonsForLearning = stats.getReasonsForLearning()\\\\n\\\\t\\\\tif (Array.isArray(reasonsForLearning) && reasonsForLearning.length > 0) {\\\\n\\\\t\\\\t\\\\tparams.onb_reasons_for_learning = reasonsForLearning\\\\n\\\\t\\\\t\\\\tparams.learning_reason = reasonsForLearning\\\\n\\\\t\\\\t}\\\\n```\\\\n\\\\nWould you like me to apply this fix to the codebase? Let me know and I can make the changes for you!\\\",\\n                  \\\"user\\\": {\\n                    \\\"name\\\": \\\"Clio (bot)\\\"\\n                  }\\n                },\\n                {\\n                  \\\"body\\\": \\\"@clio-bot Based on what you're seeing today, does it look like this is working as expected?\\\",\\n                  \\\"user\\\": {\\n ## Script Output
The following data was collected by a pre-run script. Use it as context for your analysis.

The output of the fetcher script `fetch_unified_ingest.py` is injected below:

---
If all of `slack`, `linear`, `emails`, and `telegram` outputs are empty or have no items, stop immediately. Output absolutely nothing (or just '[SILENT]') and terminate. Do not write any files, do not edit daily notes, and do not send any message.

---
### 1. Process Slack Captures (`slack`)
If there are items under the `slack` key, process them one by one:
1. Determine the reaction type: `jg_log` or `jg_decision` based on the `"reaction_type"` field in the JSON item.
2. Determine the date of the conversation (from the `ts` or messages timestamps) in YYYY-MM-DD format.
3. Determine a spaced capitalized Title based on the topic.
4. **Determine Target Folder and Path based on Reaction Type:**
   - **Path A: If reaction_type is "jg_log" (standard Slack log):**
     - Since this is an **Input**, bypass the inbox! Save the file under: `/home/justin.guest/vault/Inputs/Slack/`
     - **Filename:** `YYYY-MM-DD - Slack - [Title].md`
     - **Properties (Frontmatter):**
       ```yaml
       ---
       id: '<timestamp_id>'  # YYYYMMDDHHmmss format based on message ts
       daily_note: "[[Daily Notes/YYYY-MM-DD Weekday|YYYY-MM-DD Weekday]]"
       category: "[[Slack]]"
       channel: "<channel_name>"
       original_url: "<permalink>"
       participants:
         - "<Participant A>"
         - "<Participant B>"
       ---
       ```
     - **Body Layout:**
       Keep standard Slack logs minimalist. No point-by-point summaries, thoughts, or decisions in the body. Only:
       ```markdown
       # 📥 Slack Capture: [Title]

       - **Channel:** #<channel_name>
       - **Date:** YYYY-MM-DD
       - **Original Link:** [Slack Thread](<permalink>)

       ## Topic Description
       <A brief, 1-2 sentence Topic Description placeholder to be expanded later during Vault Jam.>
       ```
   - **Path B: If reaction_type is "jg_decision" (Decision note):**
     - Since this is a maturity-ladder note (not an Input), save it under `/home/justin.guest/vault/Inbox/` for review first!
     - **Filename:** `YYYY-MM-DD - Decision - [Title].md`
     - **Properties (Frontmatter):**
       ```yaml
       ---
       id: '<timestamp_id>'  # YYYYMMDDHHmmss format based on message ts
       daily_note: "[[Daily Notes/YYYY-MM-DD Weekday|YYYY-MM-DD Weekday]]"
       category: "[[Decisions]]"
       ---
       ```
     - **Body Layout:**
       ```markdown
       # 🏛 Decision: [Title]

       - **Date:** YYYY-MM-DD
       - **Original Link:** [Slack Thread](<permalink>)

       ## Context
       <Summarize the context of the decision from the Slack thread.>

       ## Options & Trade-offs
       <Extract pros/cons, options, and tradeoffs discussed in the thread.>

       ## Resolution
       <Detail the finalized decision and resolution, attributing it clearly to the actual decision-maker.>
       ```
5. **Daily Note Integration:**
   Append a link and one-sentence gist to today's daily note notepad under `## 🗒 Notepad`:
   - For `jg_log`: `* [[Inputs/Slack/YYYY-MM-DD - Slack - [Title]|Slack summary]]: <One-sentence-gist>.`
   - For `jg_decision`: `* [[Inbox/YYYY-MM-DD - Decision - [Title]|Decision]]: <One-sentence-gist>.`
6. **Integrations:**
   - Run the command to mark the Slack message as processed:
     `python3 ~/.hermes/scripts/fetch_slack_brains.py --mark-processed <channel_id> <ts>`
   - Run the light integration pass (appending to `Utilities/log.md` with daily note link).
   - Run `python3 ~/.hermes/scripts/integrate_entities.py <ingest_rel_path> [--gist "..."]` (e.g., `Inputs/Slack/<filename>` or `Inbox/<filename>`) to sync project hub states.

### 2. Process Linear Captures (`linear`)
If there are items under the `linear` key, process them one by one:
1. Determine the date of the comment/update (from its `createdAt` timestamp) in YYYY-MM-DD format.
2. Determine a spaced capitalized Title based on the topic.
3. Since this is an **Input**, bypass the inbox! Save the file under: `/home/justin.guest/vault/Inputs/Linear/`
4. Generate the Note Content:
   - **Filename:** `YYYY-MM-DD - Linear - [Title].md`
   - **Properties (Frontmatter):**
     ```yaml
     ---
     id: '<timestamp_id>'  # YYYYMMDDHHmmss format based on createdAt
     daily_note: "[[Daily Notes/YYYY-MM-DD Weekday|YYYY-MM-DD Weekday]]"
     category: "[[Linear]]"
     original_url: "<permalink>"
     author: "<author_name>"
     associated_with: "<external_link_to_linear_issue_or_doc>"
     ---
     ```
   - **Note Body Layout:**
     ```markdown
     # 📥 Linear Capture: [Title]

     - **Author:** <author_name>
     - **Date:** YYYY-MM-DD
     - **Original Link:** [Linear Link](<permalink>)
     - **Associated With:** [<issue_id_or_title>](<external_link_to_linear_issue_or_doc>)

     ## Topic Description
     <A high-quality 2-3 sentence Topic Description synthesizing the comment/update, the parent issue/document/project/initiative context, and its corresponding thread.>
     ```
     *Note on link formatting:* The `Associated With` section and frontmatter field MUST use an **external link** (e.g. Markdown external link `[PROD-468 - Animate correct answers in lessons](https://linear.app/...)`) pointing directly to the relevant issue, project, initiative, or doc in Linear. Do NOT use Obsidian wikilinks like `[[PROD-468]]`.
5. **Daily Note Integration:**
   Append a link and one-sentence gist to today's daily note notepad under `## 🗒 Notepad`:
   - `* [[Inputs/Linear/YYYY-MM-DD - Linear - [Title]|Linear Capture]]: <One-sentence-gist>.`
6. **Integrations:**
   - Run the command to mark the Linear item as processed:
     `python3 ~/.hermes/scripts/fetch_linear_brains.py --mark-processed <id>`
   - Run the light integration pass (appending to `Utilities/log.md` with daily note link).
   - Run `python3 ~/.hermes/scripts/integrate_entities.py Inputs/Linear/<filename> [--gist "..."]` to sync project hub states.
